## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly explicit time t, which is the standard state-space form for second-order mechanical oscillators. Nonlinear harmonic oscillators commonly include restoring forces nonlinear in x, damping terms in v (possibly nonlinear), and external or parametric forcing terms depending on t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (linear restoring force): dv_dt = -c0 * x (small-amplitude linear oscillator)
- Linear viscous damping + linear spring: dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * x (damped harmonic oscillator)
- Constant bias/tilt: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 (equilibrium shifted by constant force)
- Coulomb (dry) friction model: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * sign(v) (sliding friction approximately constant in magnitude)
- Quadratic drag damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic drag or turbulent resistance)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * x - c2 * x^3 (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Higher-order stiffness nonlinearity: dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * x - c2 * x^3 - c3 * x^5 (strongly nonlinear restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping (Rayleigh-type): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * v^2) * v - c2 * x (damping increases with speed)
- Van der Pol oscillator (state-dependent damping): dv_dt = (c0 - c1 * x^2) * v - c2 * x (self-excited oscillations / limit cycle)
- Driven oscillator (additive forcing): dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * x + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic drive)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * x - c2 * x^3 + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear resonance/chaos under forcing)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * v - (c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t)) * x (Mathieu-type parametric oscillator)
- Pendulum-like restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * v - c1 * sin(x) (angle x with nonlinear sine restoring torque)
- Potential-gradient form (conservative + damping): dv_dt = -c0 * v - d_dx(c1 * x^2 + c2 * x^4) (motion in nonlinear potential with dissipation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative oscillator signature: if dv_dt depends primarily on x (and not v), it often represents a restoring force derived from a potential U(x), i.e., dv_dt â‰ˆ -dU/dx.
- Odd symmetry restoring force: dv_dt as an odd function of x (e.g., -x, -x - x^3) indicates symmetric potentials and oscillations about x = 0.
- Damping identification: terms proportional to v (linear) or v*Abs(v) (quadratic drag) reduce energy; they appear with a sign opposing v over most of the trajectory.
- Self-excitation / limit-cycle marker: a factor like (c0 - c1 * x^2) * v implies negative damping at small |x| and positive damping at large |x|, producing stable oscillations.
- Nonlinear stiffness detection: appearance of x^3, x^5 (or sin(x)) indicates amplitude-dependent frequency (hardening/softening or pendulum effect).
- External periodic forcing: additive sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms in dv_dt indicate driven response, resonance peaks, and possible quasiperiodicity/chaos when combined with nonlinearity.
- Parametric resonance structure: time-modulated stiffness multiplying x, e.g., cos(c*t) * x, suggests Mathieu-type instability tongues rather than simple forced resonance.
- Dry friction clue: sign(v) (or v/(Abs(v)+c)) creates stick-slip-like dynamics and nonsmooth acceleration near v = 0.
- Energy-balance cue: when both nonlinear damping and nonlinear stiffness are present (e.g., Duffing + Rayleigh/Van der Pol), expect amplitude selection and harmonic distortion in trajectories.

Letâ€™s rewrite the GT in a simple polynomial-in-\(v\) and linear-in-\(x,t\) form.

### Ground Truth (GT)
Given:
\[
-0.459914680311301\,v(1-v^2)\;-\;1.87329057400732\,v\;-\;2.49934616662645\,x(0.0579034145056311\,t+1)\;-\;2.49934616662645\,x
\]

Expand:
- \( -0.459914680311301\,v(1-v^2)= -0.459914680311301\,v + 0.459914680311301\,v^3\)
- \( -2.49934616662645\,x(0.0579034145056311\,t+1)= -2.49934616662645\cdot 0.0579034145056311\,t x -2.49934616662645\,x\)

So GT is exactly:
\[
(0.459914680311301)\,v^3 \;+\;(-0.459914680311301-1.87329057400732)\,v \;+\;(-2.49934616662645-2.49934616662645)\,x \;+\;(-2.49934616662645\cdot 0.0579034145056311)\,t x
\]
Compute the combined coefficients:
- \(v^3\): \(+0.459914680311301\)
- \(v\): \(-2.333205254318621\)
- \(x\): \(-4.9986923332529\)
- \(t x\): \(-0.144715595465622\) (since \(2.49934616662645\cdot 0.0579034145056311 \approx 0.144715595465622\))

Thus GT has the exact structure:
\[
a\,v + b\,v^3 + c\,x + d\,t x
\]
with fixed \((a,b,c,d)=(-2.333205254318621,\;0.459914680311301,\;-4.9986923332529,\;-0.144715595465622)\),
and **no other terms** (no constants, no pure \(t\), no logs/exp/sin, no rational terms).

## Candidate-by-candidate analysis

### 1. \(c0*v + c1*v^3 + c2*x + c3*t*x + \frac{c4 t}{c5 t + c6} + \frac{c7}{c5 t + c6}\)

### 2. \(c0*v + c1*v^3 + c2*x^{c3} + c4*x + c5*t(c6+x)^{c7}\)
